  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_b8966535-6d2d-4c49-b319-43faf7c81344'

But the greatest threat is yet to come...<br /><br />Susan Michaels was once the hottest reporter on the Beltway Beat until she walked into a setup that ruined her reputation. Now she's working for a small Seattle paper, penning stories about killer moths and alien babies, convinced that her life couldn't get any worse...<br /><br />That was before an idea for a breaking news piece brings her to a local animal shelter where she ends up listening to her source rant about vampires and gets coerced into adopting a cat despite her allergies. But when her new pet suddenly reveals himself to be a gorgeous - and lethal - shapeshifter, Susan realizes that there's far more at stake than a career-saving by-line.<br /><br />Born into a world of predators, Were-Hunter Ravyn Kontis was betrayed by those he loved best. Soulless, pitiless, he has spent three hundred years battling the Diamons who seek to subjugate humankind. And with the ultimate battle about to begin, this one very human woman holds the power to shatter both their worlds...</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_9901207').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_9901207').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2109470502" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2109470502?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophia Triad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophia Triad" href="/user/show/44642860-sophia-triad">Sophia Triad</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2109470502" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7330602504000433721"><b>Ravyn Kontis (Dark Hunter and Arcadian Werehunter) & Susan Michaels (Human)</b><br/><br/>Have you ever watched Shrek 2? Like I have…<br/>Did you like the wicked, sneaky, cute Puss in Boots? Like I did…<br/>Did you ever wonder how Puss would look like if he was a real man and not a cat? Like I did…<br/>To be honest I always imagined that he would like Antonio Banderas (the actor that has lent his voice to the cartoon).<br/><br/>Ravyn is Kenyon’s version of Puss. His animal form is basically a kitty-cat. Susan is a reporter who saves R</span>
  <span id="freeText7330602504000433721" style="display:none"><b>Ravyn Kontis (Dark Hunter and Arcadian Werehunter) &amp; Susan Michaels (Human)</b><br /><br />Have you ever watched Shrek 2? Like I have…<br />Did you like the wicked, sneaky, cute Puss in Boots? Like I did…<br />Did you ever wonder how Puss would look like if he was a real man and not a cat? Like I did…<br />To be honest I always imagined that he would like Antonio Banderas (the actor that has lent his voice to the cartoon).<br /><br />Ravyn is Kenyon’s version of Puss. His animal form is basically a kitty-cat. Susan is a reporter who saves Ravyn from an animal shelter while he is in his animal form and takes him home – despite the fact that she is allergic to cats.<br /><br />Susan Michaels used to be the hottest reporter on the Beltway Beat, until her reputation was ruined. Now she is working for a friend of hers from college for a small newspaper writing about aliens and catpeople who transform to men and she hates every minute of her job. One day she will discover that catpeople and other strange creatures truly exist and that her friend is really a Squire for the Dark Hunters. (No, aliens are not real!)<br /><br />Ravyn on the other hand –although he appears as a fluffy kitty cat- is truly a deadly assassin who eats Daimons for breakfast. Ravyn has done a huge mistake in his past which made him hateful for his family and which transformed him into a Dark Hunter. Thus, it is hard to trust women. Susan will have a bad time with him.<br /><br />Ravyn: <i>“Honestly? I don’t want people around me for two reasons – they ultimately betray you or they die on you. Either way, you’re screwed and you spend all your time obsessing on why you didn’t see it coming. Or that you did something or didn’t do something to cause it. No offense, but I don’t like to be hurt and I’d rather just avoid it.”</i><br /><br />The book besides the story of Ravyn and Susan, also shows the world and the behavior of Squires while we learn what happened to Nick Gautier these last two years of his existence. Savitar is such a interesting character!<br /><br />Savitar: <i>“Remember, Nick, there are only two people in the universe I care for…and you’re not one of them.”</i><br /><br />For me, the book was really funny. I laughed out loud a lot.<br />My favorite character is Susan with her spunky and colorful personality. I loved the way that she interacts with Ravyn, but also with her friend Leo.<br /><br />Susan: <i>“You know, if my life was a horse, I’d shoot it.”</i><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7330602504000433721" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14910335483706386769"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You don’t knock on the devil’s door, unless you want him to answer.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Nicely developed story, many secondary storylines and characters, so much emotion, mystery and fate, love and pain, wrath, woe, guilt, and grief wrapped in one novel.The plot is exciting, well-paced, and well-worked-out with constant fights, but still followable. The final fight is excellently constructed. I loved both the humor and action in it. <br/><br/><b>Susan</b> <br/>She is irritating, bitchy, and nosy. A real smartass with sarcas</span>
  <span id="freeText14910335483706386769" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You don’t knock on the devil’s door, unless you want him to answer.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Nicely developed story, many secondary storylines and characters, so much emotion, mystery and fate, love and pain, wrath, woe, guilt, and grief wrapped in one novel.The plot is exciting, well-paced, and well-worked-out with constant fights, but still followable. The final fight is excellently constructed. I loved both the humor and action in it. <br><br><b>Susan</b> <br>She is irritating, bitchy, and nosy. A real smartass with sarcastic humor that is highly appreciated by Ravyn. But she is also brave, and a damn good fighter. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1579811737i/28830147._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>He laughed gently at her never-ending humor. Sometimes it was gallows and dark, but it never failed her. She wore it like armor.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>Ravyn</b> <br>He is a typical Dark-Hunter (Were-Hunter): dark, tall, lonely, and brooding, larded with a heartbreaking past. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1579811737i/28830148._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>He was exceptional. But it made her wonder what he’d be like if he was just an average guy on the street. No, she couldn’t imagine that. He was so much larger than life. A guy like this could never be average.</i>
</blockquote><br><b>The romance</b><br>The development of the romance seems slow because so many things happen, but actually it takes only a day for them to fall in love with each other. I loved the parallel viewpoints: when they first notice the appeal in each other, when they both think they have no chance with the other, and so on.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1579812943i/28830225._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <i>“Her kiss was tender and precious, and there in the darkness it chased away the shadows of his past and eased the pain that had lived way too long inside him.”</i>
</blockquote><br><b>Secondary Characters</b><br><br><b>Cael and Amaranda:</b> great secondary storyline, I’m really curious about them.<br><br><b>Squires and Dark-Hunters:</b> you get a glimpse into the life and work of squires.<br><br><b>Nick:</b> well, Nick is back just to cause more calamity…<br><br><b>Ash:</b> OMG, what a man!<br><br><b>Artemis:</b> What a bitch!<br><br><b>Stryker:</b> I’m starting to seriously like him.<br><br><b>Savitar:</b> hegemonic and surprisingly talkative…<br><br><br><b>
  <a href="https://exinasreadings.tumblr.com/tagged/Dark-Side-of-the-Moon" rel="nofollow noopener">My favorite quotes.</a>

<div id="review_1455632062" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1455632062" />
    <a title="Jilly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly"><img alt="Jilly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1435955932p2/25894509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1455632062?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jilly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jilly" href="/user/show/25894509-jilly">Jilly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=werewolves-and-other-furry-shifters">werewolves-and-other-furry-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25894509-jilly?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1455632062" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6241672363771240627">Most of the reviews for this are either 4-5's or 1's. I think it has to do with the personality of the main girl, Susan. Everyone either loves her or hates her. And, I'm sorry Monty, but I loved her. We usually hate the same things, but I can't resist a character that is so sarcastic that every word that comes out of her mouth is snark. It's like we are soul-mates or something. She is the ultimate smart-ass and will make wise cracks even while everything sucks. I like that.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449096640i/17232863.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Susan is a reporter fo</span>
  <span id="freeText6241672363771240627" style="display:none">Most of the reviews for this are either 4-5's or 1's. I think it has to do with the personality of the main girl, Susan. Everyone either loves her or hates her. And, I'm sorry Monty, but I loved her. We usually hate the same things, but I can't resist a character that is so sarcastic that every word that comes out of her mouth is snark. It's like we are soul-mates or something. She is the ultimate smart-ass and will make wise cracks even while everything sucks. I like that.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449096640i/17232863.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Susan is a reporter for a rag newspaper - the kind that features a disproportional amount of time and space on Bigfoot stories. She had been a respected reporter engaged to another reporter until she wrote a story without checking her sources thoroughly and was disgraced. She lost her job, her fiance, her reputation, and her home and money because of the resulting lawsuits.<br><br><b>
  <i>Groaning, she rubbed her eyes. "You know, if my life was a horse, I'd shoot it."</i>
</b><br><br>One day she ends up taking a cat home from a shelter because her cop-friend said that this cat had something to do with a conspiracy. Upon arrival, her "cat" shifts into a man, Ravyn. Ravyn is a shape-shifter and a Dark Hunter. <br><br><b>
  <i>"The last guy I had in my house could only turn into a beer drinking pig."</i>
</b><br><br>a pretty common occurrence!<br><br>Ravyn's appearance starts another shit storm in Susan's life. Now, the bad guys have the police in their control and they have framed Susan and Ravyn for the murder of Susan's best friends. So, Susan is not-so-gently introduced to the world of Dark Hunters in order to protect her.<br><br><i>
  <b>"I've got to start taking drugs," she mumbled. "At least then I'd have an explanation for all this."</b>
</i><br><br>All of this takes place in Seattle, so we get to meet new Dark Hunters and squires, but we also get a couple of old friends since they were evacuated from New Orleans since Katrina. It is interesting how Sherrilyn Kenyon worked the real-life tragedy of the hurricane into the fictional story. We even hear from Nick, who has decided that all of his problems are Acheron's fault. He has turned into a major Bitty Betty. Dude, take some responsibility for your own actions! Ash didn't put a gun to your head!<br><br>So, they are all trying to figure out why the police are working with the daimons and what they are trying to do. Hint- they are trying to kill all of the Dark Hunters in Seattle. (I guess that was more than a hint.)<br><br>I really liked this book and there were some really important bits of information for the future of the series in it. Susan cracked me up most of the time, and Ravyn was also pretty sarcastic and funny. All in all, I am disappointing my friend, Monty, who wanted me to hate Susan with her. Sorry, Monty!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449096640i/17232864._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Here's a coupon to make it better:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1449096640i/17232865.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="6241672363771240627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5831199-sita?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer186330921" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6334076113929294554">I normally love the Dark Hunter series, but I just couldn't get into this one. My faviroute scenes were the ones Nick was in. I am totally in love with him! <br/>Overall, the book was okay, I don't think you need to read it to get the story. So, if you want just skip it. It really won't matter.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1050309537" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1050309537" />
    <a title="Carmen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen"><img alt="Carmen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1050309537?book_show_action=true">Sep 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen" href="/user/show/25353295-carmen">Carmen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Kenyon fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published">traditionally-published</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=she-says">she-says</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=published2006">published2006</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1050309537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10580579316111801202">This book could have been spectacular.<br/><br/>Susan Michaels is working as a reporter for a tabloid. Two years ago she was a star investigative reporter in Seattle, chasing the big stories and winning awards. But after chasing a lead that backfired, she was disgraced. Her boyfriend of four years left her, all her friends (except Jimmy and Angie) left her, her house and car were repossessed. She's an orphan and has no family.<br/><br/>At this exceptionally low point in her life, she tried to kill herself on Thanks</span>
  <span id="freeText10580579316111801202" style="display:none">This book could have been spectacular.<br /><br />Susan Michaels is working as a reporter for a tabloid. Two years ago she was a star investigative reporter in Seattle, chasing the big stories and winning awards. But after chasing a lead that backfired, she was disgraced. Her boyfriend of four years left her, all her friends (except Jimmy and Angie) left her, her house and car were repossessed. She's an orphan and has no family.<br /><br />At this exceptionally low point in her life, she tried to kill herself on Thanksgiving while at home by herself in her roach-infested cheap apartment. Quickly realizing the mistake she made, she calls an ambulance on herself and vows to fight and live, no matter how bad things are.<br /><br />She's also conveniently a martial artist AND an ace driver. Mmmmmm-hmmmm, I'm sure. *rolls eyes*<br /><br />That's our heroine.<br /><br />Ravyn Kontis is a were-leopard who was murdered by his brother Phoenix and brought back to life by Artemis to serve her as a Dark-Hunter. Now he's a rare were-leopard/Dark-Hunter crossbreed. Unable to stand sunlight, travel through time, or teleport - he still has a lot more power than your average DH or average were-animal.<br /><br />Besides his really tragic backstory, which I will put under this spoiler tag, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ He was mated to a human female, Isabeau. After finding out what he was, she tells her family. The humans come and slaughter every woman and child in Ravyn's clan. Ravyn is blamed and his own brother Phoenix murders Ravyn, whose father Gareth spits on Ravyn and kicks his dying body. Ravyn's call for vengeance is heard by Artemis, who comes down to grant him vengeance and make him a Dark-Hunter. He slaughters Isabeau and her family and all the humans in the village. His family has never forgiven him and still shun him. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> he doesn't have much of a personality in my opinion.<br /><br />When he is trapped in his cat-body, he's put in a metriazo collar to suppress his powers and is taken to the animal shelter to be put down. Sue is called to take him by her friend Angie. Angie's detective husband Jimmy is on to some sort of Daimon conspiracy, which he tries to warn Sue about.<br /><br />Sue takes the cat home against her better judgment. She is violently allergic to cats. After taking off the cat's collar, she is surprised when he becomes a handsome, naked human man.<br /><br />...<br /><br />Great set-up, this is a great set-up. I was like "Oh, boy, let the fun adventures ensue!" Sadly, it was not to be.<br /><br />Here are the problems:<br /><br />1.) Kenyon seems to be writing this novel as a entrypoint for new readers. She spends literally at least 30% of the novel explaining everything that happened in the previous 14 books in excruciating detail. And I do mean excruciating. If you read the last 14 books (as I did) you can safely skip just about every third page in this novel. Just skip any paragraphs where some character launches into an explanation of something that has already been explained to you 1,000 times in the course of the series. This book is painful for Kenyon fans who already know her world and her mythos. She uses Susan as the "newbie" to take the place of the new reader and has everyone explain everything to Susan (the reader) as if she knew nothing.<br /><br />Very tiring.<br /><br />2.) Susan is allergic to cats. I realize that this is Kenyon trying to be cute and funny, but I didn't find this cute or funny. Ravyn makes Susan's head clog up badly, she is constantly sneezing and sniffling around him, and touching any hair of his makes her skin itch like crazy.<br /><br />And this is the man she's having sex with.<br /><br />I was cringing, this sounded so unpleasant and horrible. At one point she gives him a blowjob and I was just wincing in sympathy. The idea of doing something like that while having your nose stuffed up and runny, and also having to take breaks to sneeze uncontrollably sounds like a nightmare to me. I can't see ANYTHING pleasant about it and the fact that Ravyn stands there and lets her service him like this is just OKAY was seriously pissing me off. What a piece of shit! I was REALLY angry with him.<br /><br />Kenyon totally plays the fact that Susan's rather violently allergic to Ravyn as a hilarious joke, but the idea of her being with this man for the rest of her life when she can't even sleep in a bed next to him without being miserable is disgusting and horrifying to me.<br /><br />Finally Ravyn reaches a point where he's just like, "I'm going to shave all my hair off." I was rejoicing until Susan said, "Don't you dare!" I do not understand her reaction AT ALL and I didn't really get an explanation from Kenyon. I guess the idea she was trying to convey was that if Ravyn shaved his (waist-length) hair and body hair off, he wouldn't be attractive anymore or something. Which is bullshit. That's the least he can do since for Susan being in the same room as him is like being constantly sick. She is going to have a cold for THE REST OF HER LIFE. A never-ending head cold. This sounds like hell.<br /><br />Kenyon has a HUGE thing for long-haired men. 99% of her heroes have long, long hair that they either wear down or in a ponytail.<br /><br />3.) Romance (such as it is, with flavorless Ravyn and sneezing, suffering Sue) takes a major backseat in this book - not only to Kenyon's lengthy explanations of her world, but also to side character development. Oh, this is what's going on with Nick Gauthier, let's talk about him for three hours. Oh, Ash is having sex with that horrible evil woman again, let's talk about that for two hours. Oh, Stryker, he's evilly plotting to take Acheron down, blah blah blah.<br /><br />Listen, I don't read these stories for Kenyon's unique and elaborate take on Atlantis and Greek mythology. I read them for a good love story and good kissing and sex. Neither are delivered in this book. So it's a failure in my eyes.<br /><br />...<br />Other Notes:<br /><br /> - Susan seems to have a real chip on her shoulder about taking orders and following directions. This chip seemed to only appear when the person giving orders or directions was male. This was never explained, and I (a rabid feminist) could not really understand her knee-jerk negative reaction every time a man told her to do something. It made her seem a bit unhinged to me. I mean, she'd unload on a guy for telling her to do something when it is obvious the guy wasn't being an asshole, just making a suggestion or giving her advice or trying to keep her safe. It was unreasonable and weird. And trust me, for ME to be saying that of all people means that it really was.<br /><br /> - Susan really has a strong sense of personal responsibility. She accepts the blame for whatever happens in her life, and doesn't blame other people or God or whoever for what has happened to her. That was one of the few good things in the novel.<br /><br /> - Kenyon just HAS to slip a little bit of female self-hatred in the book, doesn't she? When Susan is introduced to an attractive female character, we get this:<br /><br /><i>Susan started to mention the fact that it was a bit nippy outside for the outfit but held her tongue. Maybe the woman would get a cold and gain some weight... At the very least, she'd cover up that perfect body so that Susan wouldn't feel quite so inadequate.<br /><br />Note to self: Start a new diet tomorrow. </i><br /><br />One, this grates my cheese. Have some respect for yourself, woman! Do you have ZERO self-esteem and self-confidence?!?!!? Jeez Louise. Two, this is pretty out of character for Susan. I mean, she just didn't NOT seem like the type of woman to have this reaction AT ALL up to this point, and then never exhibits this attitude again. Which just means that it was TOTALLY unnecessary and could have been left out of the book.<br /><br />In summary, I hated this book for a number of reasons. Feel free to skip/ignore it unless you're a huge Kenyon fan or actually care about the Nick/Acheron/Stryker subplots.<br /><br />P.S. I despised Erika. She put Ravyn and everyone else's life in danger NUMEROUS times and was SUCH a spoiled brat.<br /><br />1 REAL STAR, 2 ROMANCE STARS</span>
  <a data-text-id="10580579316111801202" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1324652140" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1324652140" />
    <a title="Gavin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin"><img alt="Gavin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1338207884p2/8192509.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1324652140?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8192509-gavin?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1324652140" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16832657246454768817">This was one of the better Dark-Hunter books in the series so far. I loved the humor and also enjoyed the fact that the romance was on a slightly slower burn than is typical with most PNR books. I felt that gave time for both Ravyn and Susan to grow attached to each other on more than just a physical level. <br/><br/>Susan is a disgraced news reporter who has been relegated to working at a paranormal focused newspaper, run by her old college friend, after a scandal cost her her career in mainstream media.</span>
  <span id="freeText16832657246454768817" style="display:none">This was one of the better Dark-Hunter books in the series so far. I loved the humor and also enjoyed the fact that the romance was on a slightly slower burn than is typical with most PNR books. I felt that gave time for both Ravyn and Susan to grow attached to each other on more than just a physical level. <br /><br />Susan is a disgraced news reporter who has been relegated to working at a paranormal focused newspaper, run by her old college friend, after a scandal cost her her career in mainstream media. Ravyn is a Were-Hunter based in Seattle. The pair meet each other when Susan tracks down a source who has a lead on a story involving the recent vampire-like slayings in the city to local animal shelter. While there she adopts a strange looking pet cat to keep her cover story in place. That cat turns out to be the Were-Hunter Ravyn who has been trapped in animal form by some new Daimon magical collar. Susan manages to unintentionally rescue him from the Daimons and is soon caught up in the happenings as the Daimons are eager to get their captive back.<br /><br />The story was humorous and fun. It was helped along by the small things like the fact that Susan is allergic to cats! Susan was a likable, strong, and surprisingly capable heroine while Ravyn was a good guy with a typically tragic back story. I thought they made a great couple and I loved the slow build of the romance as they had to learn to trust each other. <br /><br />As well as the typical Daimons Susan and Ravyn also had to deal with corrupt cops and the villainous Daimon leader Stryker. This book actually added a bit of depth to Stryker's character. We also got more progression in the overall series story arc with appearances from Savitar, Acheron, and Nick, as well as Stryker. I always enjoy it when the books in the Dark-Hunter series have a good balance between the novel story arc and the overall series story arc. <br /><br />All in all this was an enjoyable read.<br /><br />Rating: 4 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: This was narrated by Carrington MacDuffie who I always think does a good job with the series. She gets the over the top humor. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16832657246454768817" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1454047259" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1454047259" />
    <a title="Alp" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26653561-alp"><img alt="Alp" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1462791280p2/26653561.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1454047259?book_show_action=true">Nov 28, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alp" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alp" href="/user/show/26653561-alp">Alp</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26653561-alp?shelf=fantasy-romance">fantasy-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1454047259" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9404868994214438873">Dark Side Of The Moon is the ninth installment in Dark-Hunter series. As always, Sherrilyn Kenyon delivers an excellent story, a fantastic combination of Fantasy, Romance, and Action, in her own unique writing style. This book contains an interesting storyline and endearing characters.<br/><br/>Ravyn Kontis was a Were-Hunter, an Arcadian leopard, who was betrayed by his human mate and that caused him to lose his loved ones, his family, and his life. With his wrath and the need to take revenge, he became t</span>
  <span id="freeText9404868994214438873" style="display:none">Dark Side Of The Moon is the ninth installment in Dark-Hunter series. As always, Sherrilyn Kenyon delivers an excellent story, a fantastic combination of Fantasy, Romance, and Action, in her own unique writing style. This book contains an interesting storyline and endearing characters.<br /><br />Ravyn Kontis was a Were-Hunter, an Arcadian leopard, who was betrayed by his human mate and that caused him to lose his loved ones, his family, and his life. With his wrath and the need to take revenge, he became the Dark-Hunter. Since then, he had lived a life of loneliness. His family hated him and turned back on him.<br /><br />Susan Michaels was once the successful investigative reporter until she wrote one story that ruined her career because she trusted her source. She lost everything, her job, her reputation, her boyfriend, and her home. One day, she got a call from her friend, told her to go to the animal shelter for very interesting news, her whole life was turned upside down since the moment she went there, took the cat out, and brought him to her home. She was dragged into the world she never knew existed and her life was going to change forever.<br /><br />There were some unexpected moments that gave me surprises, and some sweet moments Ravyn and Susan spent together, which made me smile and feel so happy for them.<br /><br />I loved all the fight scenes in this book, they filled with excitement and danger. The romance is good, I loved that they took the time to build and develop their relationship and trust.<br /><br />I would have given this book 5 stars if I hadn't had a super big problem with Nick Gautier! I was extremely disappointed in him and I got really mad to the point where I had a wild urge to smash his teeth down his throat. I hated that he let his anger and misery blind him to his own faults. How dared he blame Acheron for his death?! He acted like a child who couldn't admit his mistakes. He didn't deserve to be a Dark-Hunter!<br /><br />However, this is a very good read and I really did enjoy it so I ended up giving 4 stars to this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9404868994214438873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText10439141343226745971" style="display:none">Ok, the ending/epilogue to this book, had me like...<br><a href="http://s1135.photobucket.com/user/Enhya77/media/tumblr_m2eg3uJFKM1qgynin_zps00084993.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

All things tie in together in some form or fashion. But with this story, with everything going on with the current plot, new plot developments, subplots &amp; the fleshing out of the main characters; nothing was too much or over the top or took away from <b>Ravyn &amp; Susan's</b> story. These two have crazy white hot chemistry together. The <i>how</i> of them crossing paths, &amp; the <i>why</i> of them becoming attached to one another was not only believable but quite touching at times. And it doesn't hurt matters that <b>Ravyn</b> is fine as hell.<br><br>This book has non stop action &amp; intrigue. LOL moments, passion, lust, love, mystery &amp; suspense galore. And some heart breaking moments too.<br><br>I would definitely recommend this read.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2324967862" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer13314064441074935273"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549739432i/27040015._SX540_.png' width='400' height='320' alt='Dark Side of the Moon' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I haven’t read a book in this series for some time. I was getting bored and tired with it. For that reason, I’m quite surprised that I liked this book as much as I actually did.<br/><br/>To be totally honest I don’t remember a lot about the previous books. Most of the time it wasn’t a problem and I caught up on the generally plot pretty easily. And to be honest I wasn’t that interested in it. The plot in just this book is not difficult to follow and it’s enjoyable. <br/><br/>One thing that I remember from the previ</span>
  <span id="freeText13314064441074935273" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1549739432i/27040015._SX540_.png" width="400" height="320" alt="Dark Side of the Moon" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I haven’t read a book in this series for some time. I was getting bored and tired with it. For that reason, I’m quite surprised that I liked this book as much as I actually did.<br><br>To be totally honest I don’t remember a lot about the previous books. Most of the time it wasn’t a problem and I caught up on the generally plot pretty easily. And to be honest I wasn’t that interested in it. The plot in just this book is not difficult to follow and it’s enjoyable. <br><br>One thing that I remember from the previous books are the overly tortured characters. Ravyn and Susan are not an exception. What’s more Susan turns out to be some sort of a warrior comparable to Dark Hunters which is totally unrealistic. But anyway, the characters in those books are rarely true-to-life. And after all, I prefer her this way rather than some weak and silly arm-candy. <br><br>As I said I enjoyed this book, it is a quick and easy read with likeable characters. Sometimes taking a break from a series seems like a good idea. It’s looks like this is the case.</span>

<div id="review_1191445999" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1191445999" />
    <a title="Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed"><img alt="Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455042547p2/22911953.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1191445999?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠" href="/user/show/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed">Monty Cupcake ☠ Queen of Bloodshed ☠</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed?shelf=tstl">tstl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed?shelf=greek-roman-mythology">greek-roman-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed?shelf=werewolves-shifters">werewolves-shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22911953-monty-cupcake-queen-of-bloodshed?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1191445999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10108611306734470055">I was excited this was another Were-Hunter book, but it's also a Dark-Hunter book. Ravyn (I thought that was a chick's name)was born a leopard/cat were & became a DH later, so he's both. <br/><br/>Susan is a disgraced reporter who now works for a tabloid. She gets suckered into taking home a cat (which is really Ravyn with a power negating collar on) & she's highly allergic to cats - yeah, hilarity ensues (no, not really). Due to this initial meeting between the two characters, the rest of the book is rif</span>
  <span id="freeText10108611306734470055" style="display:none">I was excited this was another Were-Hunter book, but it's also a Dark-Hunter book. Ravyn (I thought that was a chick's name)was born a leopard/cat were &amp; became a DH later, so he's both. <br /><br />Susan is a disgraced reporter who now works for a tabloid. She gets suckered into taking home a cat (which is really Ravyn with a power negating collar on) &amp; she's highly allergic to cats - yeah, hilarity ensues (no, not really). Due to this initial meeting between the two characters, the rest of the book is rife with <b>cat jokes</b>: "I think he has to use the litter box, " "Puss in Boots," etc. <br /><br />When the two mc's meet, Ravyn thinks she's a squire &amp; orders her about like one. Susan thinks all this supernatural stuff is a gag joke on her that her friends are pulling &amp; that Ravyn is a hired model - this means many pages of her boring inner monologue talking about what a hoax it is &amp; how she'll get her friends back. She finally realizes it's not &amp; gets pulled into the DH action &amp; world. <br /><br />The first parts before they enter the Squire/DH world reminded me of <b>Katherine Hepburn</b> &amp; Spencer Tracy in that movie where they're reporters/editors; this is not a compliment as I hate Hepubrn's annoying voice and manly attitude. Now that there's a mystery afoot!, the book reminds me of <b>Nancy Drew</b>. Now I love Nancy Drew, but the books are tediously over-detailed, archaic, and the villain is always blatantly obvious. Same thing here + that "mystery solving" methodology. There's a very juvenile feeling to it, hence the Nancy Drew reference.<br /><br />The rest of the book is more sleuthing, several villains with the evil muahaha-ing &amp; rubbing hands in glee - Dr.Evil style. The whole thing felt put upon &amp; not very creative, too obvious. They really needed Scooby &amp; the Gang on this because they figure out the villains at the last possible second. Also, Susan is <b> TSTL</b>. And I feel nothing for Ravyn. <br /><br />Other characters: <br />Nick - wtf, just wtf. Completely trashed this character, changing him from a fun &amp; loving, responsible 20-something into a whiny, bratty, bitter, vengeful, unhelpful, whiny, irresponsible, uncaring of others child. <br /><br />Stryker: He's growing on me. I can see why he gets a book later on. He's becoming a multi-faceted character vs a silly villain. <br /><br />Satara: Really? Was her presence necessary? It's too obvious, under your nose. <br /><br /><b>Acheron</b>: Well, 1. <u>No Simi appearances</u>, sadly. 2. I am so beyond effing tired of his shite shenanigans with Artemis. He's unbelievably stupid in this book, repeating mistakes he made in Seize the Night. Letting Artemis yank his chain whenever she wants. He may be 11,000 years old, but he has as much common sense as the 21 years of age he looks. <br /><br />That's all I can think of. I'm sure there's lots more that annoyed me &amp; more characters I hated, but this sums it up. I'm proud of myself for omitting the many, many f-words I wanted to use; just thinking them in my head. <br /><b>I wish I'd skipped this book</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10108611306734470055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_95015330" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95015330" />
    <a title="Leah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3050338-leah"><img alt="Leah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474253068p2/3050338.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95015330?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah" href="/user/show/3050338-leah">Leah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=m-f">m-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=adult-lit">adult-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer95015330&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95015330" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2119361333792050892">Dark Side of the Moon is the tenth book in Sherrilyn Kenyon's Dark-Hunter series. By now, I've read all but three of the full-length DH books, and there have only been three that I have not particularly cared for. Well, now there's a fourth to be added to that list. While this book had an interesting premis and the story, overall, was pretty good, the heroine was obnoxious and that affected the whole reading experienced for me.<br/><br/>The heroine, Susan, was constantly (and I mean <i>constantly</i>) making som</span>
  <span id="freeText2119361333792050892" style="display:none">Dark Side of the Moon is the tenth book in Sherrilyn Kenyon's Dark-Hunter series. By now, I've read all but three of the full-length DH books, and there have only been three that I have not particularly cared for. Well, now there's a fourth to be added to that list. While this book had an interesting premis and the story, overall, was pretty good, the heroine was obnoxious and that affected the whole reading experienced for me.<br /><br />The heroine, Susan, was constantly (and I mean <i>constantly</i>) making some kind of quip about what was doing. Now, I can respect sarcasm and humor in a woman, in anyone, but Susan was a little over the top for me.<br /><br />I liked Ravyn, though. He was a cutie and a sweetheart. However, I felt that he told her about himself and trusted Susan too easily. All of the Dark-Hunters have felt betrayal; that's how they got to be Dark-Hunters in the first place. That being said, they have the tendency not to trust very easily and not be quite so open with their pasts. While it's true that Susan found out about his past from Dorian, Rave's brother, Ravyn answered her questions a little too honestly to be realistic in the beginning. Why would you tell a complete stranger your secrets?<br /><br />I thought it was ridiculous that Susan was allergic to Ravyn. At first, it was kind of funny, but after that, I just wanted to shoot one of them to put me out of my misery. I don't really want to hear about how she's sneezing up a storm while she's trying to have sex with Ravyn.<br /><br />I loved the Squires and other Dark-Hunters. It was really nice to see Otto again after Seize the Night, and I loved Kyl and Leo. The Dark-Hunter Zoe was pretty hilarious, and I liked Cael, even if it was weird for me that he was married to an Apollite woman.<br /><br />So, Ravyn is the only Dark-Hunter who doesn't want his soul back? Yeah, that was a bit ridiculous, too, in my opinion. Why on earth wouldn't he want to be free of that bitch Artemis so that he could just live his life with Susan?<br /><br />Nick Gautier, that little shit, needs to leave Acheron alone. I can understand Nick being bitter and angry about his mother dying and his becoming a Dark-Hunter, but I in no way appreciate him blaming Ash for everything, especially Hurricane Katrina. Ash can only do so much people! Even he has rules! That being said, though, I know that Nick gets hooked up with Satara (the bitch) and Stryker somehow and it was nice to see how he got roped into that.<br /><br />Also, I was pleasantly surprised to see a little bit of a nicer, softer side of Stryker. Now, I know that he's in no way this nice guy, but it's always nice to see the super baddie have a little bit of a soft side.<br /><br />Overall the book was okay, but it's not one of the Dark-Hunter books that I would rush to re-read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2119361333792050892" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText15872651893444129857" style="display:none">I read this one sometime last month and was supposed to write a review for it but RL has been kind of crazy so it somehow slipped through the cracks.<br /><br />It's the story of a Were-Hunter, Ravyn, who finds himself in quite a pickle that Susan, a disgraced reporter, unwittingly gets him out of. A good friend of hers has asked her to visit her at the animal shelter she works at for a story, and makes her adopt a cat before she leaves.<br /><br />The story sounded crazy, but when the cat she adopted changes into a lethal man that saves her life, she has to open her mind to all kinds of things she didn't believe were real before.<br /><br />Her world turned upside down, Susan is now firmly in Ravyn's world, where vampires exist and so do shifters and daimons, and a centuries long war has been taking place that she and most of humanity knew nothing about.<br /><br />Eventually, Susan uses her investigative reporter skills to help Ravyn uncover the truth about the increased daimon activity and the recent death of a Dark-Hunter in the region. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[A police chief with a wife and two sons who turned daimon, is determined to avenge the death of his wife at the hands of Ravyn, so has allied with the daimons to take the Dark-Hunters down. <div id="review_377331321" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/377331321" />
    <a title="AJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3143126-aj"><img alt="AJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406382884p2/3143126.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/377331321?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="AJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="AJ" href="/user/show/3143126-aj">AJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=paranormal-uf">paranormal-uf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=romantic">romantic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3143126-aj?shelf=lol">lol</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer377331321" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17859208537687014932">OMFG!!! She’s done it to me again!! I settled in for what I knew would be a great PNR book, thinking that it would be a quick and easy read - I should have known better. Yes, I slipped straight back into Kenyon’s incredible world, but an easy read… not so much, I was flipping pages madly and my heart was pounding through most of it. I can’t think of another author I’ve read who puts so much story into her stories, it’s just amazing. I can’t believe everything that happened in this book! This is </span>
  <span id="freeText17859208537687014932" style="display:none">OMFG!!! She’s done it to me again!! I settled in for what I knew would be a great PNR book, thinking that it would be a quick and easy read - I should have known better. Yes, I slipped straight back into Kenyon’s incredible world, but an easy read… not so much, I was flipping pages madly and my heart was pounding through most of it. I can’t think of another author I’ve read who puts so much story into her stories, it’s just amazing. I can’t believe everything that happened in this book! This is the tenth book in the Dark Hunter series, and in addition to the story told in this book, the story arcs continue from previous books, as well as new storylines starting. <br /><br />This book was primarily about Ravyn, the swoony Were / Dark Hunter who is described early on in the book as “<i>sex on a stick</i>”. Yeah, I’ve gotta agree with that! I loved his character. Apart from his paranormal abilities and his undead-ness (yes that’s a word, I just made it up), he seemed so much like a real guy. His actions and his dialogue were so believable, and he wasn’t over the top in his Alpha-ness, and I really liked that. <br /><br />Susan was also a great character, with lots of sass and sarcastic humour, and the two of them were perfect together. Their love story seemed real and believable, and I loved that they had a true friendship in addition to the romance. <br /><br />We got to understand a lot more about the Squire part of the world in this book, which I enjoyed, and there were a lot of new characters, in addition to lots of characters re-appearing from previous books. Thank God for Sherrilyn Kenyon’s website with its database of characters (and cheers to Aestas for hooking me up with it) – it helps keep everybody straight and I’d probably be a bit lost otherwise! <br /><br />I loved seeing Nick come back into the action, but am in disbelief at what is going on with him. Where is that going to go? And Cael! His story was tragic, and again left me wondering what’s going to happen there? Stryker provided a few surprising moments, and I'm keen for more of his story. Savitar’s cameo was brilliant as always, and had me laughing out loud. And then there’s my beloved Acheron who showed up, and was more tortured than ever <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[his confrontation with Nick absolutely broke my heart! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Part of me dreads getting to his book because I can’t bear to see him suffer any more, but then again, I need to see him get his HEA. He’s such an amazing character.<br /><br />I love this series! Kenyon makes me feel so strongly for her characters, that each book and every little twist is absolutely heart wrenching. But she adds in great action, laugh out loud moments and sensationally swoony romance and I just can’t get enough! Love it!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17859208537687014932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_37768972" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37768972" />
    <a title="Sandi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/811687-sandi"><img alt="Sandi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404709147p2/811687.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37768972?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sandi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sandi" href="/user/show/811687-sandi">Sandi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780312357436" href="/book/show/685455.Dark_Side_of_the_Moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/811687-sandi?shelf=2008">2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/811687-sandi?shelf=cross-genre">cross-genre</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37768972" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7879214767870495357">I found the hardcover edition "Dark Side of the Moon" for $5.99 on the Borders bargain books rack. Sherrilyn Kenyon has a lot of books in print and seems to be quite popular. I'm not into the whole vampire lover genre, but for $5.99, I figured I could at least see what made Kenyon so popular. I must now shamefully admit that I really enjoyed "Dark Side of the Moon". I could have done without the whole gods/daimons/Dark Hunters/Appolites/etc. back story, but I loved the character of Susan. I love</span>
  <span id="freeText7879214767870495357" style="display:none">I found the hardcover edition "Dark Side of the Moon" for $5.99 on the Borders bargain books rack. Sherrilyn Kenyon has a lot of books in print and seems to be quite popular. I'm not into the whole vampire lover genre, but for $5.99, I figured I could at least see what made Kenyon so popular. I must now shamefully admit that I really enjoyed "Dark Side of the Moon". I could have done without the whole gods/daimons/Dark Hunters/Appolites/etc. back story, but I loved the character of Susan. I loved her sarcastic, spunky attitude. I liked how she reacted to the weirdness around her much like I would have. The romance between her and Ravyn was good too. It was entirely predictable, but enjoyable nonetheless. I rarely like sex scenes in books because 99% of them are so poorly written, they're both awkward and funny. However, the scenes between Susan and Ravyn were very well done. I blush to even say that. <br /><br />In some ways, "Dark Side of the Moon" reminded me of "Buffy the Vampire Slayer" TV series. It was sexy, funny and had girl-power. I don't know if the rest of the Dark Hunter books are anything like this. Frankly, I really don't want to read anything more about Acheron. I would like to read stories about Zoe or Belle, two Dark Hunters who appear only briefly. I'd like to know more about what happens to Erika. I'd like to follow up with Cael and Amaranda. I wonder if there's anyway to pick and chose the characters I'd like to learn more about.<br /><br />By the way, I gave this only 3 stars because it's not particularly original and it's pretty trashy (in a good way). It would get another half star if we had them. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7879214767870495357" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_203068363" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/203068363" />
    <a title="TJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2346207-tj"><img alt="TJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596753171p2/2346207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/203068363?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TJ" href="/user/show/2346207-tj">TJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2346207-tj?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer203068363" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12607031616648732429">2.5/5.0<br/><br/>This is the first book in the "Dark Hunter" series that I honestly didn't think held up to Kenyon's exacting standards. It's perplexing, too. Her stories are usually tight, well put together, her world building understandable, her characters empathetic and believable - even though often-times incredibly dark and tortured. All of those makings were present in this book, they just never came to fruition.<br/><br/>Take the main reason we read these books, the romance. Susan and Ravyn are both characte</span>
  <span id="freeText12607031616648732429" style="display:none">2.5/5.0<br /><br />This is the first book in the "Dark Hunter" series that I honestly didn't think held up to Kenyon's exacting standards. It's perplexing, too. Her stories are usually tight, well put together, her world building understandable, her characters empathetic and believable - even though often-times incredibly dark and tortured. All of those makings were present in this book, they just never came to fruition.<br /><br />Take the main reason we read these books, the romance. Susan and Ravyn are both characters we grow to love and cheer for individually. We just can't muster the energy to cheer for them <i>together</i>. Ravyn's impression of Susan is mild, she's attractive but nothing to turn his head. Susan's <i> allergic</i> to Ravyn! (He's a were-leapard and she's allergic to cats) She can't stand to even be close to him without erupting into sneezing fits. As time progresses, they find they have tragic pasts in common and seem to get along well. When faced with the possibility of being mated, both are actually annoyed and disappointed they might be stuck together for eternity. How are we supposed to buy into this romance if the characters aren't even buying into it?!? Even as things ratchet up and a declaration is imminent, Ravyn claims he <i> might be </i> falling in love with her. That's it!! The story never once gives us a reason to believe in this romance. We have A plus B equals D... we're missing C, folks!!<br /><br />This is also the first time I have actually been confused over the intricacies of Kenyon's world. Things were assumed but not explained, other things were left hanging, some were just plain confusing. For instance, there is a scene where a daimon (I'm really trying not to spoil here) breathes into a dark-hunter and turns him into a daimon. I didn't know one could do that. It has never even been alluded to in all the books before. That little ability is BIG, why didn't the daimons do this LONG before now? It would have changed EVERYTHING in their world! Absolutely NOTHING was explained. <br /><br />Over-all this book was head-shaking confusing in all areas and that is SO unlike Kenyon. Hopefully this is a fluke and her next story will be back on track and scrumptiously entertaining again.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12607031616648732429" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_128603557" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4365117-emily?shelf=genre-paranormal">genre-paranormal</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer128603557" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4375396848820153659">When Dark Hunter/Were Shifter Ravyn gets himself hauled off to the pound he thinks perhaps his time maybe up. When he is adopted by a woman who appears to be allergic to cats, he prods her to get the collar that is keeping him in cat form off in order to gain back his strength.<br/><br/>Susan Michaels went from a dynamic journalist to writing about aliens and creatures for a tabloid, after one wrong lead ruined her career. When her best friend calls her to the pound to share some news, she ends up with a </span>
  <span id="freeText4375396848820153659" style="display:none">When Dark Hunter/Were Shifter Ravyn gets himself hauled off to the pound he thinks perhaps his time maybe up. When he is adopted by a woman who appears to be allergic to cats, he prods her to get the collar that is keeping him in cat form off in order to gain back his strength.<br /><br />Susan Michaels went from a dynamic journalist to writing about aliens and creatures for a tabloid, after one wrong lead ruined her career. When her best friend calls her to the pound to share some news, she ends up with a cat and stuffed up nose. Susan realizes her life has just changed as the cat transforms to a chiseled naked man in her front room. The fun is just beginning as he becomes the hunted rather than the hunter.<br /><br />Ton of fun, plus it had Savitar, Nick, Otto some of my favorites from the series. The one thing about this one is I noticed there were several side stories with Nick, Cael, and a few others. Love her books.</span>

<div id="review_33606310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/33606310" />
    <a title="MelissaB" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1320046-melissab"><img alt="MelissaB" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1245899832p2/1320046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/33606310?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="MelissaB" class="user" itemprop="url" name="MelissaB" href="/user/show/1320046-melissab">MelissaB</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">dark hunter fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1320046-melissab?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1320046-melissab?shelf=darkhunters">darkhunters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer33606310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7427051706041766399">This book was a little slow in the beginning but really picked up about a quarter of the way through.<br/><br/>Ravyn and Susan were an interesting couple. Ravyn was a very hot Dark Hunter/Arcadian Were Hunter. He, of course, had some issues. His family killed him about 300 years ago after he told his potential mate that he was a Were Hunter, which caused her to gather a group of humans to attack Ravyn's villiage and kill some of his pack including his mother and sister. His brother killed him for his "bet</span>
  <span id="freeText7427051706041766399" style="display:none">This book was a little slow in the beginning but really picked up about a quarter of the way through.<br /><br />Ravyn and Susan were an interesting couple. Ravyn was a very hot Dark Hunter/Arcadian Were Hunter. He, of course, had some issues. His family killed him about 300 years ago after he told his potential mate that he was a Were Hunter, which caused her to gather a group of humans to attack Ravyn's villiage and kill some of his pack including his mother and sister. His brother killed him for his "betrayal", which caused Ravyn to become a Dark Hunter when he cried out to Artemis for his vengence against the humans. Susan is a disgraced reporter who works for a sleezy magazine similar to the National Enquirer. She used to be one of the nation's top investigative reporters until she trusted the wrong source and had her life go down in flames (Dan Rather?). Susan meets Ravyn when she picks him up at an animal shelter at the request of her friend. Ravyn is stuck in cat form because of a magical collar and if he doesn't change soon, he will die. Susan gets the collar off of him and the bad guys start showing up. This is where the story started to get interesting.<br /><br />Susan and Ravyn are fighting the Daimons that seriously have it in for the Dark Hunters. Ash is nowhere to be found (haha, I read Acheron so I know where he was, why he was there and why he couldn't leave!). During all of the fighting, Ravyn and Susan somehow find time to fall for each other, despite the fact that she is allergic to him :) After they do some mattress dancing, they get the magical markings that say they are mates. So basically, the rest of the book was fighting with Daimons while trying to figure out what their master plan was, as well as Ravyn and Susan trying to figure out their relationship aka do we wanna be mates?<br /><br />I really liked Ravyn in the book, I am a sucker for a hot shapeshifter. Susan's unending sarcastic remarks got on my nerves at first but I started to warm up to her, though I still don't think she could have been the great Daimon fighter she was depite the karate she took years ago. I think I understood this book a lot better because of reading the first half of Acheron before this book. I know who Appollymi is and why she is in Kalosis, I know Ash's background and why he lets the "bitch goddess" treat him the way she does (plus I know he will be free of her and no longer have to pay in flesh and blood for love). Overall, it was a decent book but still doesn't hold a candle to Acheron.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7427051706041766399" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_690681532" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/690681532" />
    <a title="v.v" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12242315-v-v"><img alt="v.v" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1503177013p2/12242315.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/690681532?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="v.v" class="user" itemprop="url" name="v.v" href="/user/show/12242315-v-v">v.v</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12242315-v-v?shelf=my-all-time-favourite">my-all-time-favourite</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer690681532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8874586088979996580">To be honest this wasn't the most memorable book in this series. I knew going in I wouldn't be too interested because I didn't know any of the characters that well. Don't get me wrong, this book was still pretty good but not up to par with others in the series. A problem that most other readers had was with Susan. She can come off as a bitch or a little insecure at times and that makes her irritating, or you could have loved her sarcastic, kick ass self. I was more in the later. I also found som</span>
  <span id="freeText8874586088979996580" style="display:none">To be honest this wasn't the most memorable book in this series. I knew going in I wouldn't be too interested because I didn't know any of the characters that well. Don't get me wrong, this book was still pretty good but not up to par with others in the series. A problem that most other readers had was with Susan. She can come off as a bitch or a little insecure at times and that makes her irritating, or you could have loved her sarcastic, kick ass self. I was more in the later. I also found some parts weird weird but funny. For example, how she's allergic to cats but fell in love with a werecat. Very ironic!<br><br><br>The characters were much more fleshed out than some other books because once again there was less mythology and more romance and character development. Susan was full of sarcasm no matter how dire the situation. She could be facing evil demons or having an allergic reaction and she could still bring on the snark. It was very entertaining. Paired with Ravyn's quiet humor and brooding mood, they balanced and complimented each other. Ravyn was more withdrawn than expected, for me at least. He was an unusual mix of wereanimal and dark hunter, making a him a being of unnatural power, and he was hated because his mate lead the deaths of many members of his clan. He reminds me a lot of Spawn. Hopefully we'll get a story about him as well. I loved meeting other characters such as Phoenix, and meeting old characters like Bryanna, who I know from CON. Nick was back, but not his usual Cajun self. He is angry and putting a lot of blame both on Ash and himself. And he is starting to come off a little whiny. This book takes place in Seattle which adds a nice change of scenery and it was nice to see how Kenyon wove Hurricane Katrina into her world. <br><br><br>The story was full of action, obviously and was full of witty humor. I may be getting a little irritated by the sarcasm because it happens so often and sometimes in the wrong spot. But it does good in action scenes and suits characters like Susan. Love, pain, hate and so many emotions are wrapped up in a wonderful package.<br><br> <br><br>Just look at this quote:<br><br><i> "I've got to start taking drugs," she mumbled. "At least then I'd have an explanation for all this." </i><br><br> <br> Overall it was a 4.5 star rating!<br><br>Full Review at <a href="http://wintereading.blogspot.ca/" rel="nofollow noopener">Wintereading</a><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456708772i/18268428.png" width="300" height="100" alt="/&gt;" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="8874586088979996580" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UPiOzTX05m+ZlvQYS55bqoLW4PcK4wTb88X4MMo620Vmpr5vktpugxT+HVLv8qdwh1RsGm4qQufmaGxoJ0vG3Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('7BeWou452G0p6oGlm4ZAeImM3bW3hvIPTzdLNjriC/DaSaYASRdQgaSCaO8/6ryijA5RWNNPtDNamt9u15MWaA==')})
  }
